2003-12-17: marcel@hsdev.com: ChangeSet 1.1799
  Transparently upgrading core modules. This is somewhatdifficult to test. What i tested:- manually setting version number in db to some bogus valueresult: works sometimes, depending on the switch use in theupgrade function, some upgrade functions return false when theactual upgrade wasn't necessary. Guess thats good, although wecould recover automatically in these specific situations- rolled back the repository a couple of weeks, this triggeredupgrades (downgrades actually) for some core modules. Almostnone of them allowed downgrading (dd and authsystem did, so i took those)then rolled forward to current bk and applied the patchdd and authsystem were mentioned as successfully upgrade on top ofthe list. The remaining core modules signalled an upgrade although theirversion number was the same in the db, as in the file system. This wasa remnant of my testing, and not fatal, because i could successfully "upgrade" them.I've tried to come up with a situation where transparent upgrading would fail; theoretically they should go through the upgrade.php.The disadvantage i can see is that an admin who is already late with hisbackup of the database ((s)he should have done it before copying over the code) does not get a chance to look at the upgrade code before upgrading..del-patch-2003-12-17-08-51-54~36f71a08548af019:  Delete: PATCHES/patch-2003-12-17-08-51-54

2003-12-17: andyv@andyv.local: ChangeSet 1.1796
  minor correction
  	* html/modules/modules/xartemplates/admin-list.xd:
	  slightly different approach to miko's - we just declare block level container's height to avoid using clearing element, which may (and would) interfere with css only themes. Decided to put in below the body javascript to keep js together.Weir language javascript. Mozilla seems to be very strict with this.

2003-12-06: andyv@andyv.local: ChangeSet 1.1722
  this was one of the most horrible examples of templates i ever came across in xaraya core (took me 30 min to analyse and 10 min to correct, so it _deserves_ a couple of comments)1. the intention of using floats for form layout is (generaly speaking) good, but the implementation was too casual for any practical value, with high potenitial of breaking themes (containing floats principle was neglected)2. the implementation of <option> tags was totally unacceptable - php shorthand of the worst kind - reading and debugging of such templates is highly problematic due to the fact that tags are left _unclosed_ inside xar:if constructs then closed with odd number, thus leaving a text-editor no chance to balance all tags properly and produce _readable_ sourcenote: this template needs to be re-visited at a later stage with purpose of removing inline styles (to be substituted with upcoming xsg rules)
  	* html/modules/blocks/xartemplates/admin-modify_instance.xd:
	  major corrections

2003-12-02: ccorliss@lxwdev-1.schwabfoundation.org: ChangeSet 1.1694
  - fix to allow instances to be taken into account when deciding access rights-- Someone please double check :)
  	* html/modules/privileges/xarprivileges.php:
	  - fixes problem where instances are never taken into account when deciding access rights  - problem originates from incorrect assumption of expression: value = array1 + array2    in this expression, if the arrays are both numerical, only indices with unique values    will be added to the resultant array. ie:     array1 = (0 => 'All', 1 => 'test');    array2 = (0 => 'Something', 2 => 'Else');    value = array1 + array2;    value == (0 => 'All', 1 => 'test', 2 => 'Else')    notice how 'Something' disappeared. It's because, when adding them together this way,    indices with the same value will not overwrite each other (goes for number based indices only    afair).
